Instruction: Explain how moneyline betting works on Polymarket sports markets
Response: Moneyline betting on Polymarket involves predicting which team will win outright regardless of the margin of victory. For favorites, negative odds like -165 mean you must risk $165 to win $100 in profit, while for underdogs, positive odds like +135 mean risking $100 wins $135 in profit. This straightforward bet type is ideal for strong favorites where you're confident in the win but not the margin, and Polymarket displays these as binary outcome markets with YES/NO shares priced accordingly.

Instruction: Explain the concept of moneyline betting on Polymarket sports markets
Response: Moneyline betting on Polymarket involves predicting the outright winner of an event, disregarding the margin of victory. Favorites are represented by negative odds, such as -165, indicating a $165 risk to win $100 in profit. Conversely, underdogs are denoted by positive odds, like +135, meaning a $100 risk yields $135 in profit. This straightforward bet type is suitable for strong favorites where confidence in the win is high but the margin is uncertain, and Polymarket displays these as binary outcome markets with YES/NO shares priced accordingly.

Instruction: Explain the concept of moneyline betting on Polymarket sports markets
Response: When betting on Polymarket sports markets using moneyline odds, the goal is to predict which team will win outright, regardless of the margin of victory. For favorites, negative odds like -165 signify that a $165 risk is required to win $100 in profit. Underdogs, on the other hand, are represented by positive odds, such as +135, indicating that a $100 risk results in $135 in profit. This type of bet is ideal for situations where a strong favorite is expected to win but the margin is uncertain, and Polymarket presents these as binary outcome markets with YES/NO shares priced accordingly.

Instruction: Explain what American odds format means on Polymarket
Response: American odds on Polymarket use positive and negative numbers to indicate favorites and underdogs. Negative odds like -280 indicate a favorite where you risk $280 to win $100, while positive odds like +240 indicate an underdog where risking $100 wins $240. The larger the negative number, the heavier the favorite; the larger the positive number, the bigger the underdog. These odds directly correlate to share prices in Polymarket's binary markets.

Instruction: Explain how point spreads work on Polymarket sports betting
Response: Point spreads on Polymarket level the playing field by requiring favorites to win by more than a specified margin. For example, a team with -8.5 must win by 9 or more points to "cover the spread," while the underdog at +8.5 covers by losing by 8 or less or winning outright. Spread markets typically show odds around -110 on both sides, meaning you risk $110 to win $100, with the half-point preventing tie scenarios called pushes.

Instruction: Explain what covering the spread means on Polymarket
Response: Covering the spread on Polymarket means the team you bet on performs better than the point spread requires. A favorite at -6.5 covers by winning by 7 or more points, while an underdog at +6.5 covers by losing by 6 or fewer points or winning the game. Unlike moneyline bets focused on who wins, spread betting rewards accurate margin prediction and is Polymarket's way of creating balanced markets where both outcomes have near 50-50 odds.

Spread betting on Polymarket rewards accurate margin predictions, creating balanced markets where both outcomes have roughly equal odds.

Instruction: Explain how totals or over/under betting works on Polymarket
Response: Totals betting on Polymarket involves predicting whether the combined score of both teams will be over or under a specified number. For a total of 236.5, betting over wins if the combined score is 237 or higher, while under wins if it's 236 or lower. The half-point total prevents push scenarios where the exact number is hit, and Polymarket presents this as a binary market with over and under as the two outcomes.

Instruction: Explain the concept of totals betting on Polymarket.

Instruction: Explain the concept of totals betting on Polymarket.
Response: On Polymarket, over/under betting for totals markets works as follows: if the combined score of both teams is 237 or higher, over wins, while under wins if the combined score is 236 or lower. The half-point total eliminates the possibility of a push when the exact number is hit, and the market is presented as a binary choice between over and under.

Instruction: Explain what first half (1H) betting markets are on Polymarket
Response: First half betting markets on Polymarket settle based solely on the score at halftime, offering faster resolution than full-game bets. Options include 1H moneyline (which team leads at halftime), 1H spreads (margin at halftime), and 1H totals (combined halftime score). These markets typically feature spreads and totals roughly half of full-game lines and attract traders looking for reduced exposure time or those identifying teams with strong or weak starts.

Instruction: Explain how to calculate implied probability from American odds on Polymarket
Response: To calculate implied probability from American odds on Polymarket, use different formulas for favorites and underdogs. For negative odds like -200, divide the odds by (odds + 100), giving -200/(-200+100) = 66.67% implied probability. For positive odds like +150, divide 100 by (odds + 100), giving 100/(150+100) = 40% implied probability. This conversion helps compare Polymarket share prices to traditional sportsbook odds and identify value opportunities.

Instruction: To determine implied probability on Polymarket, apply distinct formulas for favorite and underdog odds. For positive odds, like +150, use the formula 100 divided by the sum of the odds and 100.

Instruction: Explain what vig or juice means in Polymarket sports betting
Response: Vig (vigorish) or juice on Polymarket represents the commission or fee built into betting markets, similar to traditional sportsbooks. When both sides of a spread show -110 odds, the bookmaker's vig is embedded in that 10-cent difference from even money. On Polymarket, the vig manifests as the bid-ask spread in the order book, where market makers profit from the difference between buying and selling prices while providing liquidity to traders.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket incorporates vig or juice into its sports betting markets.
Response: Polymarket's vig, or juice, represents the commission built into betting markets, similar to traditional sportsbooks. When both sides of a spread show -110 odds, the bookmaker's vig is embedded in that 10-cent difference from even money. This manifests on Polymarket as the bid-ask spread in the order book, where market makers profit from the difference between buying and selling prices while providing liquidity to traders.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket incorporates vig or juice into its sports betting markets.
Response: Polymarket's vig, also known as juice, is the commission or fee embedded in its betting markets. This is comparable to traditional sportsbooks, where the vig is often represented by a 10-cent difference from even money, signified by -110 odds on both sides of a spread. On Polymarket, the vig appears as the bid-ask spread in the order book, allowing market makers to profit from the difference between buying and selling prices while maintaining market liquidity.

Instruction: Explain what player props are on Polymarket sports markets
Response: Player props (proposition bets) on Polymarket are binary markets focused on individual player performance rather than game outcomes. Examples include whether a player scores over/under a certain point total, records a specific stat milestone, or achieves a particular feat during a game. These markets allow Polymarket traders to leverage specialized knowledge about player matchups, recent form, or injury situations independently from team-level betting.

Instruction: Explain how parlays work in sports betting on Polymarket
Response: Parlays on Polymarket involve combining multiple bets where all selections must win for the parlay to pay out. While traditional sportsbooks offer parlay builders, Polymarket traders can create similar positions by holding shares across multiple markets. The key difference is that Polymarket allows early exit by selling individual positions, whereas traditional parlays are all-or-nothing. Correlated parlays link outcomes from the same game, like a team winning and the total going over.

Instruction: Explain the concept of parlays on Polymarket and how they differ from traditional sportsbook parlays.
Response: Parlays on Polymarket involve combining multiple bets where all selections must win for the parlay to pay out. Unlike traditional sportsbooks, Polymarket traders can create similar positions by holding shares across multiple markets, allowing for early exit by selling individual positions. This contrasts with traditional parlays, which are all-or-nothing. Correlated parlays on Polymarket link outcomes from the same game, such as a team winning and the total going over.

Instruction: Explain what futures betting means on Polymarket
Response: Futures betting on Polymarket involves predicting season-long outcomes like championship winners, playoff qualifiers, or award recipients before and during the season. These markets remain open for extended periods, allowing traders to enter or exit positions as team performance and injury situations evolve. Polymarket's liquid markets with real-time pricing let futures traders lock in profits or cut losses by selling shares before season conclusion, unlike traditional sportsbooks where futures bets are typically held until settlement.

Instruction: Explain what a push means in Polymarket sports betting
Response: A push on Polymarket occurs when the final result lands exactly on the betting line, typically in spread or totals markets without half-points. For example, if the spread is -6 and the favorite wins by exactly 6 points, it's a push where neither side wins. However, most Polymarket sports markets use half-point lines like -6.5 or 236.5 to eliminate push scenarios, creating definitive YES or NO outcomes that align with the platform's binary market structure.

Instruction: Explain the concept of a push in the context of Polymarket sports betting markets.
Response: A push on Polymarket happens when the final result matches the betting line exactly, usually in spread or totals markets without half-points. For instance, if the spread is -6 and the favorite wins by 6 points, it's a push where neither side wins. Most Polymarket sports markets use half-point lines like -6.5 or 236.5 to prevent push scenarios, ensuring YES or NO outcomes that fit the platform's binary market structure.

Instruction: Explain what the hook means in Polymarket point spreads
Response: The hook on Polymarket refers to the half-point added to spreads and totals to prevent push scenarios. Lines like -6.5, +3.5, or over 236.5 include the hook, forcing a definitive winner. Without the hook, a -6 spread pushed if the favorite wins by exactly 6, creating ambiguity. Polymarket's binary market structure strongly favors half-point lines since every market needs a clear winning outcome for proper share redemption at resolution.

Instruction: Explain the concept of the hook in Polymarket point spreads

Without the hook, a -6 spread would push if the favorite wins by exactly 6, creating ambiguity. Polymarket's binary market structure heavily relies on half-point lines since every market requires a clear winning outcome for proper share redemption at resolution.

Instruction: Explain the concept of the hook in Polymarket point spreads
Response: On Polymarket, the hook is a half-point added to spreads and totals to prevent push outcomes. This results in lines such as -6.5, +3.5, or over 236.5, which guarantee a clear winner. In contrast, a -6 spread without the hook would push if the favorite wins by exactly 6, leading to uncertainty. Instruction: Explain how bankroll management applies to Polymarket sports betting
Response: Bankroll management on Polymarket involves allocating a specific percentage of your total capital to each sports bet rather than risking arbitrary amounts. Common strategies include flat betting (same dollar amount per bet), percentage-based staking (1-5% of bankroll per bet), or Kelly Criterion sizing based on your perceived edge. Proper bankroll management prevents ruin during inevitable losing streaks and allows Polymarket traders to sustain long-term profitability across hundreds of sports market trades.

Instruction: Explain what expected value (EV) means in Polymarket sports betting
Response: Expected value on Polymarket sports markets measures the theoretical profit or loss from a bet when repeated many times. Calculate EV by multiplying each outcome's probability by its profit/loss and summing them. If you assess a team has a 60% win chance but Polymarket shares trade at 50 cents, the positive EV suggests a profitable long-term bet. Consistent positive EV betting is the foundation of professional sports trading on Polymarket.

Instruction: Explain what game props are on Polymarket
Response: Game props on Polymarket are proposition bets on specific in-game events rather than final outcomes, such as whether there will be a safety, which team scores first, or whether the game goes to overtime. These binary markets allow traders to leverage situational knowledge about team tendencies, coaching styles, or game scripts. Game props offer diverse betting opportunities beyond traditional spreads and totals, often with less efficient pricing since they're harder for models to predict.

Instruction: Explain how odds correlate to share prices on Polymarket
Response: Traditional sportsbook odds directly correlate to Polymarket share prices through implied probability. A -110 line (52.4% implied probability) converts to roughly 52-cent shares on Polymarket, while +200 odds (33.3% implied) translate to approximately 33-cent shares. However, Polymarket's dynamic CLOB pricing may offer better or worse prices than traditional books depending on order flow, allowing traders to capture arbitrage when Polymarket pricing diverges from fair value established by sportsbook consensus.

Instruction: Explain what home field advantage means for Polymarket odds
Response: Home field advantage on Polymarket sports markets is typically worth 2-3 points in spreads across major sports, reflecting benefits like crowd support, familiar conditions, and reduced travel fatigue. Markets automatically price in this advantage, so a neutral-site matchup between the same teams would show different spreads than a home game. Polymarket traders should understand that home advantage varies by sport, team, and venue, with some teams showing stronger home splits than the typical market adjustment.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket accounts for home field advantage in sports odds.
Response: Polymarket's sports markets typically assign a 2-3 point value to home field advantage in spreads across major sports, encompassing benefits such as crowd support, familiar conditions, and reduced travel fatigue. This advantage is automatically factored into Polymarket's pricing, leading to differing spreads for neutral-site matchups versus home games. Polymarket traders should be aware that home advantage can differ significantly by sport, team, and venue, with some teams displaying stronger home splits than the typical market adjustment.

Instruction: Explain what contrarian betting means on Polymarket
Response: Contrarian betting on Polymarket involves taking positions opposite the public consensus, betting underdogs when the crowd heavily favors favorites or fading over-hyped teams. This strategy exploits public biases and overreactions captured in Polymarket's order flow. Since the platform's prices reflect marginal trader beliefs, identifying when casual money creates mispricing allows contrarian traders to buy shares at artificially inflated or deflated prices before markets correct toward true probability.

Instruction: Explain how weather affects Polymarket sports totals
Response: Weather significantly impacts Polymarket totals markets, particularly in outdoor sports like football and baseball. Wind, rain, and extreme temperatures typically lower expected scoring, pushing sharp traders toward under bets. Polymarket totals initially set by market makers may not fully adjust for late-breaking weather forecasts, creating value opportunities. Traders monitoring weather reports can identify when conditions will suppress offense more than current total lines reflect, especially in wind-heavy or precipitation-affected games.

Instruction: Explain what reverse line movement means on Polymarket
Response: Reverse line movement on Polymarket occurs when the market price moves opposite to the betting volume, indicating sharp money overwhelming public action. If 70% of traders back Team A but the spread moves in Team B's favor, it signals that large, sophisticated positions on Team B are outweighing numerous small public bets. This pattern helps Polymarket traders identify where sharp money sits and potentially indicates the winning side, though it's not infallible.

Instruction: Explain the concept of reverse line movement on Polymarket, including its implications for traders.
Response: On Polymarket, reverse line movement occurs when the market price contradicts the betting volume, indicating that large, informed positions are overpowering smaller public bets. This is evident when, for instance, 70% of traders back Team A but the spread moves in Team B's favor, suggesting that sophisticated investors are outweighing numerous small public wagers. This pattern helps Polymarket traders identify areas where sharp money is active and potentially indicates the winning side, though it's not foolproof.

Instruction: Explain what middle opportunities are in Polymarket betting
Response: Middle opportunities on Polymarket arise when line movement allows traders to take both sides at different numbers, creating a chance to win both bets. If you buy shares at -3.5 and the line moves to -7.5, buying the other side creates a middle where both positions win if the final margin is 4, 5, 6, or 7 points. While middles are rare and require line movement, Polymarket's ability to take positions across time makes middling more achievable than simultaneous same-line betting.

However, Polymarket's order book structure means a few large sophisticated positions can offset many small public bets, making volume dollars more important than bet count percentages.

Instruction: Explain what team total bets are on Polymarket
Response: Team total bets on Polymarket focus on a single team's score rather than the combined total, asking whether Team A scores over or under a specific point threshold like 27.5. These markets allow traders to isolate opinions about one team's offensive capability against the opposing defense, independent of what the other team does. Team totals provide additional betting angles when you have strong conviction about one side's performance but uncertainty about the opponent.

Instruction: Explain what halftime betting lines are on Polymarket
Response: Halftime betting lines on Polymarket are new markets created at halftime based on current game state, offering fresh spreads, totals, and moneylines for the second half only. These lines account for first-half performance, momentum, adjustments, and game script. Halftime markets let Polymarket traders capitalize on information unavailable pre-game, like team energy, coaching adjustments, or player performance, though liquidity may be lower due to the compressed trading window.

This is especially valuable around key numbers in football where buying across 3 or 7 significantly increases win probability.

Instruction: Explain what quarter and period betting are on Polymarket
Response: Quarter and period betting on Polymarket involves markets that settle based on individual quarters in basketball/football or periods in hockey rather than full games. The compressed timeframes reduce variance compared to full games while allowing multiple betting opportunities within a single event on Polymarket.

Instruction: Explain what bad beats mean in Polymarket sports betting
Response: Bad beats on Polymarket occur when you lose a bet that appeared virtually certain to win, typically due to unlikely late-game events. Examples include a favorite covering until a meaningless garbage-time touchdown pushes the margin under the spread, or a total going over on a final second shot. While psychologically painful, bad beats are part of variance in sports betting, and Polymarket traders must focus on long-term expected value rather than individual unfortunate outcomes.

Instruction: Describe the concept of bad beats in the context of Polymarket sports betting.
Response: Bad beats on Polymarket occur when a bet that seemed almost guaranteed to win ultimately loses due to an unexpected late-game event. This can happen when a favourite covers the spread until a meaningless score is scored in garbage time, or when a total goes over due to a last-second shot. While bad beats can be frustrating, they are a natural part of variance in sports betting, and Polymarket traders must focus on long-term expected value rather than individual losses.

Instruction: Explain what closing line value means for Polymarket traders
Response: Closing line value (CLV) on Polymarket measures whether you got better odds than the market's final price at game time, serving as a validation metric for bet quality. If you bought shares at 45 cents and the closing price is 55 cents, you achieved positive CLV of 10 cents, indicating your early position was sharper than market consensus. Consistent positive CLV correlates strongly with long-term profitability, making it a key performance indicator for serious Polymarket sports traders.

Instruction: Explain the significance of closing line value in the context of Polymarket trading.
Response: On Polymarket, closing line value (CLV) measures whether you secured better odds than the market's final price at game time, serving as a validation metric for bet quality. For instance, if you bought shares at 45 cents and the closing price is 55 cents, you achieved a positive CLV of 10 cents, indicating your early position was more accurate than market consensus. Consistent positive CLV strongly correlates with long-term profitability, making it a key performance indicator for Polymarket traders.

Instruction: Explain the significance of closing line value in the context of Polymarket trading.
Response: Polymarket uses closing line value (CLV) as a metric to assess the quality of bets. CLV indicates whether you obtained better odds than the market's final price at game time. If you purchased shares at 45 cents and the closing price is 55 cents, your CLV would be 10 cents, signifying that your early position was more informed than market consensus. A consistent positive CLV is strongly associated with long-term profitability, making it a crucial metric for serious Polymarket traders.

Instruction: Explain what a trap game means in Polymarket betting
Response: A trap game on Polymarket occurs when a favorite playing a seemingly inferior opponent is overlooking them due to a bigger upcoming game, creating upset risk. These games often feature inflated spreads as the public hammers the favorite, while sharp Polymarket traders identify the underdog value. Recognizing trap games requires analyzing team schedules, motivation levels, and coaching tendencies, with opportunities arising when market prices don't reflect the favorite's potential lack of focus.

Instruction: Describe the concept of a trap game in the context of Polymarket betting.
Response: A trap game on Polymarket occurs when a heavily favored team is overlooking a seemingly weaker opponent due to a more significant upcoming match, creating a risk of an upset. This often results in inflated point spreads as the public heavily bets on the favorite, while savvy Polymarket traders recognize the value in the underdog. To identify trap games, one must analyze the teams' schedules, motivation levels, and coaching tendencies, and look for opportunities where market prices do not accurately reflect the favorite's potential lack of focus.

Instruction: Explain what Polymarket sports market liquidity means for traders
Response: Sports market liquidity on Polymarket determines how easily you can enter and exit positions at favorable prices without significant slippage. High-liquidity markets with $100k+ volume offer tight spreads and large order books allowing instant fills, while low-liquidity markets may require limit orders and patience. Polymarket traders should check liquidity before sizing positions, as attempting large trades in thin markets can result in poor execution prices and wider effective spreads than displayed.

Instruction: Explain the significance of liquidity in Polymarket sports markets for traders.

Conversely, low-liquidity markets may necessitate patience and limit orders, potentially resulting in poor execution prices and wider effective spreads. Traders should assess liquidity before placing large trades on Polymarket to ensure optimal price execution.

Instruction: Explain what reduced juice means on Polymarket compared to sportsbooks
Response: Reduced juice on Polymarket occurs when the platform's CLOB structure creates tighter spreads than traditional sportsbook vig. Instead of paying -110 on both sides (implying 4.5% vig), Polymarket's competitive market making might offer -105 equivalent or better, reducing the house edge. This improved pricing accumulates significantly over many bets, making Polymarket potentially more profitable for sports traders than traditional books, especially on high-liquidity markets where bid-ask spreads compress to minimal levels.

Instruction: Explain the difference in juice between Polymarket and traditional sportsbooks
Response: On Polymarket, reduced juice occurs when the platform's competitive market making creates tighter spreads than traditional sportsbooks, resulting in lower vig. This can be seen in the reduced odds, for example, -105 instead of -110, which reduces the house edge. Polymarket's reduced juice can make it more profitable for sports traders, especially on high-liquidity markets with minimal bid-ask spreads.

Instruction: Explain the difference in juice between Polymarket and traditional sportsbooks
Response: Polymarket's reduced juice is a result of its CLOB structure, which enables competitive market making and tighter spreads compared to traditional sportsbooks. This means that instead of paying -110 on both sides, Polymarket's reduced juice can offer -105 or better, reducing the house edge. Over many bets, this improved pricing can make Polymarket more profitable for sports traders, particularly on high-liquidity markets with compressed bid-ask spreads.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket calculates prices, including the role of market makers and the relationship between prices and probabilities
Response: On Polymarket, prices are calculated based on real-time supply and demand. When a market is created, market makers (traders placing limit orders) set the initial price by matching YES and NO orders at $1.00, which is then converted into one share each. The prices displayed are the midpoint of the bid-ask spread unless the spread is over $0.10, in which case the last traded price is used. The prices also reflect probabilities, with the probability displayed as the midpoint between the bid and ask price. However, buyers may not always be able to purchase shares at the displayed price due to the bid-ask spread.

Instruction: Describe the process by which Polymarket determines its prices, including the contributions of market makers and the relationship between prices and probabilities.

Prices also reflect probabilities, with the probability displayed as the midpoint between the bid and ask price. Instruction: Explain how to use the Order Book on Polymarket
Response: On Polymarket, the Order Book is a list of open orders to buy or sell shares in a particular market. It displays the highest price traders are willing to pay (bids) and the lowest price they are willing to accept (asks). The gap between the highest bid and the lowest ask is called the spread. To manage open orders, you can view them on the market's page and cancel them by clicking the red x button. Additionally, you can monitor all open orders across multiple markets from the Portfolio page.

Instruction: Describe the functionality of the Order Book on Polymarket
Response: On Polymarket, the Order Book showcases open buy and sell orders for a specific market, displaying the highest bid and lowest ask prices. The spread is the difference between these two prices. Open orders can be viewed and canceled from the market's page by clicking the red x button. The Portfolio page also allows monitoring of open orders across multiple markets.

Instruction: Describe the functionality of the Order Book on Polymarket

The spread is the price gap between the highest bid and lowest ask. To manage open orders, navigate to the market's page and click the red x button to cancel. Alternatively, the Portfolio page offers a comprehensive view of open orders across multiple markets.

Response: Polymarket does not impose strict trading size limits, but executing large trades can be difficult due to the potential impact on market prices. The orderbook matches buyers and sellers, but the absence of willing counterparties and liquidity can affect transactions. Before trading, it's crucial to examine the orderbook to understand the market's liquidity depth.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket handles user wallet management.
Response: When using Polymarket, users are prompted to create a wallet, which is a 1 of 1 multisig on Polygon controlled by their accessing EOA. This proxy wallet holds their positions (ERC1155) and USDC (ERC20). Using proxy wallets allows Polymarket to provide a seamless experience with atomic multi-step transactions and gas optimization. Developers can access positions programmatically through the smart contract wallet or transfer assets to a new address using the owner account.

Instruction: Explain how to get markets on Polymarket
Response: On Polymarket, retrieving markets can be done by utilizing the central limit order book (CLOB) functionality. The CLOB is a crucial component of the Polymarket platform, providing a comprehensive overview of all available markets. By using the CLOB interface, users can access information on market status, clients, authentication, pricing, spreads, and order manipulation, allowing them to place single or multiple orders, retrieve order details, and more.

Instruction: Explain how to withdraw money from Polymarket
Response: On Polymarket, withdrawing money is a simple, instant, and free process. However, when withdrawing USDC.e, it is swapped for native USDC through the Uniswap v3 pool due to a less than 10bp difference in output amount. In cases where the pool is exhausted or for extremely large deposits with limited liquidity, you can try breaking the withdrawal into smaller amounts or waiting for the pool to rebalance. Alternatively, you can select to withdraw USDC.e directly, but be aware that some exchanges may no longer allow direct deposits of USDC.e.

Instruction: Explain how to get active orders on Polymarket using CLOB API
Response: On Polymarket's CLOB API, you can retrieve active orders for a specific market using the get_orders endpoint. This requires a L2 Header. To use this endpoint, provide the market ID as a parameter, as well as optional parameters such as order ID, asset ID, and more. The response will return a list of open orders filtered by the provided market. You can implement this functionality in your Python or Typescript code using the py_clob_client library.

Instruction: Explain the Polymarket Real-Time Data Socket (RTDS) in a few sentences
Response: Polymarket's Real-Time Data Socket (RTDS) is a WebSocket-based streaming service that provides real-time updates for various Polymarket data streams, allowing clients to subscribe to multiple data feeds simultaneously. The RTDS supports two types of authentication and users can dynamically subscribe to and unsubscribe from topics and filters without disconnecting from the socket. The service can be used with a Typescript client, which can be downloaded and viewed here.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket tokenizes its outcomes using Conditional Token Framework (CTF) on the Polygon network.
Response: On Polymarket, all outcomes are tokenized on the Polygon network using Gnosis' Conditional Token Framework (CTF). The tokenization process involves creating binary outcome tokens for 'YES' or 'NO' results, which are represented as distinct ERC1155 tokens related to a parent condition and backed by the same collateral. The token IDs are derived from the condition ID, collection IDs, and index sets, which are calculated based on the oracle, question ID, outcome slots, and outcome slot count. This enables Polymarket to leverage the CTF contract for 'splitting' and 'merging' full outcome sets, providing a secure and efficient way to manage tokenized outcomes.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket utilizes the Conditional Token Framework (CTF) on the Polygon network for outcome tokenization.
Response: On Polymarket, binary outcome tokens for 'YES' or 'NO' results are created and represented as distinct ERC1155 tokens related to a parent condition and backed by the same collateral. The token IDs are derived from the condition ID, collection IDs, and index sets, which are calculated based on the oracle, question ID, outcome slots, and outcome slot count. This enables Polymarket to leverage the CTF contract for 'splitting' and 'merging' full outcome sets, providing a secure and efficient way to manage tokenized outcomes.

Instruction: Explain the purpose and key benefits of the Polymarket Relayer Client.
Response: The Polymarket Relayer Client enables builders to route on-chain transactions through Polymarket's Polygon relayer infrastructure, offering several benefits, including gasless transactions, safe wallet deployment, token approvals, and Conditional Token Framework (CTF) operations. This allows users to deploy safe wallets, set token allowances, and execute CTF operations, such as splitting, merging, and redeeming positions, as well as monitor transaction status and track transaction metadata.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket uses rate limiting to manage API requests.
Response: Polymarket uses Cloudflare's throttling system to enforce general rate limits on API requests. When a user exceeds the maximum allowed rate for an endpoint, requests are delayed or queued rather than immediately rejected. Bursts above the sustained rate are allowed in some cases, and rate limits reset based on sliding time windows. Polymarket sets varying limits for different endpoints, ranging from throttling requests over the maximum configured rate to specific counts per second or minute, such as 2400 requests per 10 seconds or 12000 requests per 10 minutes.

Instruction: Explain how to use Polymarket Websocket to connect to the Market or User channel
Response: To connect to the Market or User channel using Polymarket Websocket, you will need to first derive API keys from your Polymarket account. This can be done using a Polymarket Proxy associated with an Email/Magic account or a Browser Wallet (e.g. Metamask, Coinbase Wallet). Once you have obtained the API keys, you can use them to initialize a ClobClient and connect to the Websocket using a WebSocketApp. The client must be configured to match your login method, and the API keys must be used to authenticate the connection. Once connected, you can subscribe to the Market or User channel to receive real-time updates.

Instruction: Explain how disputes are resolved on Polymarket
Response: On Polymarket, disputes are resolved through a process that involves checking the proposed market resolution for errors. If no one challenges the proposal within a 2-hour challenge period, it's deemed valid, and the proposer receives their bond back plus a reward. However, during this period, anyone can dispute the proposal by posting a challenge bond of the same amount as the proposer's bond, starting a debate period of 24-48 hours. After this, UMA token holders vote, and one of four outcomes determines the resolution: the proposer wins, the disputer wins, the event is deemed too early, or the outcome is unknown/50-50, in which case the market price resolves to 50% yes and 50% no.

Instruction: Describe the Polymarket dispute resolution process
Response: On Polymarket, disputes are resolved through a process involving error checks on proposed market resolutions. If no one challenges the proposal within a 2-hour window, it's deemed valid, and the proposer receives their bond back plus a reward. However, during this period, anyone can dispute the proposal by posting a challenge bond of the same amount as the proposer's bond, initiating a 24-48 hour debate period. Following this, UMA token holders vote, and one of four outcomes determines the resolution: the proposer wins, the disputer wins, the event is deemed too early, or the outcome is unknown/50-50, resulting in a market price of 50% yes and 50% no.

Instruction: Describe the Polymarket dispute resolution process
Response: Polymarket resolves disputes through a multi-step process. First, proposed market resolutions are reviewed for errors. If no one contests the proposal within a 2-hour window, it's considered valid, and the proposer receives their bond back along with a reward. However, during this time, anyone can dispute the proposal by matching the proposer's bond amount, triggering a 24-48 hour debate period. After this, UMA token holders vote, and one of four possible outcomes determines the resolution: the proposer wins, the disputer wins, the event is deemed too early, or the outcome is unknown, resulting in a 50-50 market price.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket resolves disputes between market participants
Response: On Polymarket, disputes are resolved through a process involving error checks on proposed market resolutions. If no one challenges the proposal within a 2-hour window, it's deemed valid, and the proposer receives their bond back plus a reward. However, during this period, anyone can dispute the proposal by posting a challenge bond of the same amount as the proposer's bond, initiating a 24-48 hour debate period. Following this, UMA token holders vote, and one of four outcomes determines the resolution: the proposer wins, the disputer wins, the event is deemed too early, or the outcome is unknown/50-50, resulting in a market price of 50% yes and 50% no.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket resolves disputes between market participants
Response: Polymarket resolves disputes through a multi-step process. First, proposed market resolutions are reviewed for errors. If no one contests the proposal within a 2-hour window, it's considered valid, and the proposer receives their bond back along with a reward. However, during this time, anyone can dispute the proposal by matching the proposer's bond amount, triggering a 24-48 hour debate period. After this, UMA token holders vote, and one of four possible outcomes determines the resolution: the proposer wins, the disputer wins, the event is deemed too early, or the outcome is unknown, resulting in a 50-50 market price.

This process involves providing your Polygon account's CLOB API key, secret, and passphrase. Only connections to the user channel necessitate this authentication, and it's essential to ensure a secure and authorized connection for your Polymarket interactions.

Instruction: Explain how to place the first order on Polymarket using the provided clients.
Response: To place your first order on Polymarket, you'll need to use one of their two clients, either the Python client (py-clob-client) or the Typescript client. After installing the client, you'll need to fill in the necessary constants at the top of the code, such as your private key and Polymarket proxy address. You can then use the client to create and sign a limit order. For example, to buy 5 tokens at a price of 0.01, you'll need to specify the token ID and provide the necessary credentials. The client will take care of the rest, including sending the order to the Polymarket API. It's worth noting that there are two types of clients: one that uses a Polymarket proxy and another that trades directly from an EOA (external account). The choice of client depends on your login method.

Instruction: Explain how to redeem tokens in Polymarket after payouts have been reported.
Response: After payouts have been reported in Polymarket, users with shares in the winning outcome can redeem their tokens for underlying collateral. This is done by calling the redeemPositions function on the CTF contract, which burns valuable conditional tokens in return for collateral according to the reported payout vector. In Polymarket, users can specify the condition to redeem using the indexSets parameter, which represents a nontrivial partition of the outcome slots of the given condition. Specifically, each element in the array represents the outcome collection, with 1|2 being a common example in the Polymarket case.

Instruction: Describe the redemption process in Polymarket after payout reporting is complete.
Response: After payouts have been reported in Polymarket, users can redeem their tokens for underlying collateral by calling the redeemPositions function on the CTF contract, which burns conditional tokens in return for collateral according to the reported payout vector. The indexSets parameter allows users to specify the condition to redeem, representing a nontrivial partition of the outcome slots of the given condition.

Instruction: Describe the redemption process in Polymarket after payout reporting is complete.
Response: In Polymarket, users with shares in the winning outcome can redeem their tokens for collateral by invoking the redeemPositions function on the CTF contract. This process involves burning conditional tokens in exchange for collateral, with the payout vector determining the collateral amount. Users can specify the condition to redeem using the indexSets parameter, which represents a partition of the outcome slots.

Instruction: Explain how to recover a missing deposit on Polymarket

Alternatively, for Polygon deposits, go to https://matic-recovery.polymarket.com/. This ensures you can recover your assets efficiently. Polymarket provides these tools to facilitate easy recoveries.

Users can submit proposals via the #market-suggestion channel on Discord or by tagging @polymarket on Twitter/X, providing the best chance of being listed.

Instruction: Explain how to subscribe to receive real-time market updates through the Polymarket Market Channel and what types of messages can be received from this channel.
Response: Polymarket's Market Channel allows you to subscribe to real-time market updates through a WebSocket connection. You can receive several kinds of messages, including 'book' messages that update the current order book, 'price_change' messages that are triggered by new orders or cancelled orders, 'tick_size_change' messages when the minimum tick size of a market changes, and 'last_trade_price' messages when a maker and taker order is matched. These messages contain information such as asset IDs, market conditions, prices, sizes, and timestamps, allowing you to stay informed about market activity in real-time.

Instruction: Describe the process of subscribing to Polymarket's Market Channel to receive live market updates and the types of messages that can be received.

These messages contain asset IDs, market conditions, prices, sizes, and timestamps, providing subscribers with timely market activity information.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket streams real-time crypto prices for various trading pairs.
Response: Polymarket streams real-time crypto prices for various trading pairs through its Real Time Data Stream (RTDS) service. The service provides updates for cryptocurrency prices from two different sources, Binance and Chainlink oracle networks. Binance source delivers real-time price data using lowercase concatenated pairs, while Chainlink source delivers price data using slash-separated pairs. Both streams support various trading pairs, and price updates are sent as market prices change. The timestamp in the payload represents when the price was recorded, and the outer timestamp represents when the message was sent via WebSocket.

These updates aim to enhance the overall user experience and provide more functionality to users.

Instruction: Explain how limit orders work on Polymarket
Response: Polymarket allows users to create limit orders, which are open orders that only execute when the market trades at the user's desired price. This means that users can set a specific price they're willing to pay for a share of a market, and if the market reaches that price, the order will be filled. Partially filled orders are also possible, where traders can buy or sell parts of the user's order. Users can manage their limit orders on the market's page or in their portfolio, and they can be automatically cancelled in certain situations, such as in sports markets when the game starts. To cancel a limit order, users can simply click the red x button alongside the order.

Instruction: Explain how to place multiple orders in batch using the Polymarket API.
Response: Polymarket's CLOB supports batch orders, allowing you to place up to 15 orders in a single request. To place multiple orders in batch, you need to create a PostOrders array containing the orders you want to place, each with its own order object, order type, and owner. The order object includes parameters such as the order salt, maker, signer, taker, token ID, maker amount, taker amount, expiration, nonce, and fee rate basis points. You can choose from different order types, including Fill-Or-Kill (FOK), Fill-And-Kill (FAK), Good-Til-Cancelled (GTC), and Good-Til-Date (GTD). After creating the PostOrders array, you can use the post_orders endpoint to place the orders in batch.

Instruction: Explain how to interpret the OrderFilled event on Polymarket in relation to an on-chain transaction.
Response: When you see an OrderFilled event on Polymarket, it means that a trade has been executed on-chain, resulting in the exchange of assets between a maker and a taker. The maker is the user who initiated the order, and the taker is the user who fulfilled it, receiving the agreed-upon asset. The event also includes information about the assets involved in the trade, such as the amount of the maker's asset given out and the amount of the taker's asset received. This event helps you understand the on-chain activity on Polymarket, enabling you to track trades and asset movements in real-time.

A prediction market is a trading mechanism where market participants buy and sell claims or predictions on future events or outcomes, with prices determined by aggregate expectations. Polymarket enables users to create and trade on markets related to diverse topics, facilitating speculation, information aggregation, and rewards for accurate predictions. The platform utilizes a unique mechanism to resolve markets, ensuring users receive rewards for correct predictions or incur losses for incorrect ones.

Instruction: Explain how to add Polymarket order attribution for a builder on an order placement flow
Response: To add Polymarket order attribution for a builder, the builder attribution system allows you to attach custom headers to customer orders before posting them to the CLOB. This enables Polymarket to attribute orders to your specific builder account, providing visibility into which orders originate from your platform. You can use either remote or local signing methods to sign orders and add authentication headers. The @polymarket/builder-signing-sdk package handles all signing and header injection automatically, making it easy to implement secure order placement with builder attribution on Polymarket.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket calculates its Holding Rewards
Response: Polymarket distributes Holding Rewards based on the total position value of eligible positions. The rewards are calculated daily, using a 4.00% annualized rate, and are randomly sampled hourly. The total position value is determined by the current shares and the most recent mid-price for each outcome in eligible markets. This approach aims to keep long-term pricing accurate and is currently funded through the Polymarket Treasury.

The total position value is determined by the current shares and the most recent mid-price for each outcome in eligible markets, funded through the Polymarket Treasury.

Instruction: Explain how the comment subscription feature works in Polymarket, including support for real-time updates on comment-related events.
Response: In Polymarket, the comments subscription feature provides real-time updates on various comment-related events. These events can include the creation of new comments, reactions to existing comments, and replies to other comments. When subscribed to comments, users receive messages with a defined structure that includes fields for the comment's body, creation timestamp, and user information. The comment hierarchy is supported with nested threading, allowing for top-level comments and replies. This feature can be used for real-time comment feeds, discussion thread monitoring, and community sentiment analysis in Polymarket.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket's Central Limit Order Book works
Response: Polymarket's Central Limit Order Book is a hybrid-decentralized order book system that combines off-chain order management with on-chain settlement. It allows for the creation, listing, and execution of orders for binaryOutcome Tokens (CTF ERC1155 assets and ERC20 PToken assets) and collateral assets (ERC20). Orders are EIP712-signed structured data, and matched orders have one maker and one or more takers, with price improvements benefiting the taker. The operator handles off-chain order management and submits matched trades to the blockchain for execution, ensuring security and fairness through the use of an audited Exchange contract and symmetric fee structures.

Instruction: Describe Polymarket's Central Limit Order Book architecture.

Orders are EIP712-signed structured data, and matched orders have one maker and one or more takers, with price improvements benefiting the taker. An audited Exchange contract and symmetric fee structures ensure security and fairness. Off-chain order management is handled by the operator, who submits matched trades to the blockchain for execution.

Instruction: Explain how Liquidity Rewards work on Polymarket
Response: Polymarket's Liquidity Rewards Program allows users to earn money by placing limit orders that contribute to the market's liquidity and balance. The reward amount depends on the helpfulness of the user's orders in terms of size and price compared to others. Users can earn more rewards by placing competitive limit orders and helping the market stay active. Rewards are paid out daily based on the user's contribution to the market, and can be viewed in real-time on the Rewards page. The minimum reward payout is $1, with amounts below this threshold not being paid out.

Instruction: Explain how prediction markets work, specifically in the context of Polymarket.
Response: Polymarket is a platform for prediction markets. In a prediction market, people bet on the outcome of future events by buying and selling shares in the outcomes, which collectively forecast the likelihood of events. The price of shares in a prediction market represents the current probability of an event happening. If an event occurs, each share becomes worth a certain amount, yielding a profit. This allows market prices to continuously reflect the most current and accurate probabilities, often being more accurate than traditional polls and expert predictions.

The price of shares reflects the current probability of an event occurring. If the event happens, each share becomes worth a certain amount, resulting in a profit. This dynamic pricing allows market prices to accurately reflect the most current probabilities, often surpassing the accuracy of traditional polls and expert predictions.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket operates and why it uses crypto, specifically USDC.
Response: Polymarket is a prediction market platform that operates on a decentralized blockchain, specifically on the Polygon network built on Ethereum. It uses the USDC stablecoin, pegged 1:1 to the US Dollar, for all transactions. This architecture offers a stable medium for trading, shields users from cryptocurrency volatility, and ensures fairness and open participation globally. The platform facilitates transparent and regulated transactions, backed by reserved assets, which fosters trust and accuracy in prediction markets.

Instruction: Explain how to use the Polymarket Order Manipulation API to Get Order by ID.
Response: On Polymarket's Order Manipulation API, you can retrieve a specific order by providing its ID. This is achieved through the 'Get Order' endpoint, which requires a valid L2 Header. The request parameters include the 'id' of the order, which is a string. The response format includes an 'order' object, which is an OpenOrder and contains various fields detailing the order's status, size, price, and more. You can use client libraries, such as Python or Typescript, to interact with the API and retrieve the desired order information.

This endpoint requires a valid L2 Header and includes the 'id' parameter in the request. The response is an 'order' object, which is an OpenOrder containing fields for status, size, price, and more.

Instruction: Explain how trades can be fetched on Polymarket, including the various states a trade can be in.
Response: On Polymarket, all historical trades can be fetched via the CLOB REST API. A trade is initiated when a "taker" creates a marketable limit order, which can be matched against one or more resting limit orders on the associated book. Trades can have various statuses, including MATCHED, MINED, CONFIRMED, RETRYING, and FAILED. In some cases, due to gas limitations, a trade may be broken into multiple transactions, resulting in separate trade entities with a bucket_index and match_time field. These trade entities can be reconciled client-side by combining objects with the same market_order_id and match_time, and incrementing bucket_index.

Instruction: Describe the process of retrieving historical trades on Polymarket, including the possible states a trade can be in.

Trades can have different statuses: MATCHED, MINED, CONFIRMED, RETRYING, and FAILED. Due to gas limitations, a trade may be split into multiple transactions, resulting in separate trade entities with a bucket_index and match_time field. These trade entities can be reconciled client-side by combining objects with the same market_order_id and match_time, and incrementing bucket_index.

Instruction: Explain how to use embeds on Polymarket, including the steps for Substack and Web
Response: On Polymarket, you can embed a live-updating widget displaying the latest odds for markets on the web. To do this, navigate to the individual market you want to embed, click the 'embed' link, select light or dark mode, and copy the generated code. Then, paste the code into your code editor or CMS and publish as normal. For Substack, navigate to any Polymarket market, right-click to get the URL, and paste it into the compose window. The embeds feature currently supports single markets only, so you can't embed a combination of markets like "Most Gold Medals at Paris Olympics". The Polymarket link will be converted to a widget that automatically refreshes with the latest odds in your newsletter.

Instruction: Explain Polymarket Gamma, a hosted service for market resolution
Response: Polymarket Gamma is a hosted service that indexes market data from UMA 0.0 requests and provides additional metadata, including categorization, indexed volume, etc. This service is made available through a REST API, and is accessible to public users who can use it to fetch useful information about markets for non-profit research projects, alternative trading interfaces, automated trading systems, and more. The Gamma service is hosted at https://gamma-api.polymarket.com, offering a read-only resource for fetching market data and metadata.

Instruction: Explain the role of a builder in Polymarket
Response: On Polymarket, a 'builder' refers to a person, group, or organization that routes orders from their customers to Polymarket. This can include unique front ends that allow users to place trades on Polymarket through their system. Builders have two main benefits: they gain access to Polygon relayer, allowing gasless transactions and Safe wallet deployment, and they can add custom headers to trading orders for clear attribution, which can result in high-volume builders being showcased in the Builder Leaderboard and eligible for Polymarket grants.

Instruction: Explain the position of a builder within the Polymarket ecosystem
Response: On Polymarket, a 'builder' is an entity that facilitates order routing from their users to the platform. This can involve creating custom interfaces for placing trades on Polymarket. Builders have two key advantages: they gain access to the Polygon relayer, enabling gasless transactions and Safe wallet deployment, and they can add custom headers to trading orders for clear attribution, which may result in prominent display on the Builder Leaderboard and eligibility for Polymarket grants.

Instruction: Explain the position of a builder within the Polymarket ecosystem
Response: In the context of Polymarket, a builder is an intermediary that forwards client orders to the platform. This can include bespoke interfaces for placing trades on Polymarket. Builders benefit from two main features: they can utilize the Polygon relayer for gasless transactions and Safe wallet deployment, and they can add custom metadata to trading orders for clear attribution, which can lead to high-volume builders being featured on the Builder Leaderboard and making them eligible for Polymarket grants.

Instruction: Describe the role of a builder on the Polymarket platform
Response: On Polymarket, a 'builder' is an entity that facilitates order routing from their users to the platform. This can involve creating custom interfaces for placing trades on Polymarket. Builders have two key advantages: they gain access to the Polygon relayer, enabling gasless transactions and Safe wallet deployment, and they can add custom headers to trading orders for clear attribution, which may result in prominent display on the Builder Leaderboard and eligibility for Polymarket grants.

Instruction: Describe the role of a builder on the Polymarket platform
Response: In the context of Polymarket, a builder is an intermediary that forwards client orders to the platform. This can include bespoke interfaces for placing trades on Polymarket. Builders benefit from two main features: they can utilize the Polygon relayer for gasless transactions and Safe wallet deployment, and they can add custom metadata to trading orders for clear attribution, which can lead to high-volume builders being featured on the Builder Leaderboard and making them eligible for Polymarket grants.

Users should be cautious of potential scams and refer to official Polymarket communication channels for accurate information.

Instruction: Explain Polymarket's Liquidity Rewards Program
Response: Polymarket's Liquidity Rewards Program is a system designed to incentivize healthy and liquid marketplaces. The program provides rewards to liquidity providers based on their participation in markets, including boosts for two-sided liquidity and a reduced rate for single-sided liquidity. The rewards are calculated using a formula that takes into account the orders' position between the adjusted midpoint and the minimum qualifying spread. The overall goal of the program is to catalyze a healthy and liquid marketplace by creating incentives for liquidity providers, encouraging trading activity, and discouraging exploitative behaviors.

Instruction: Explain the key features of Polymarket's Liquidity Rewards Program.

The rewards are calculated using a formula that considers the orders' position between the adjusted midpoint and the minimum qualifying spread. This program aims to promote trading activity and discourage exploitative behaviors.

Instruction: Explain how to cancel orders in Polymarket
Response: In Polymarket, you can cancel orders using the API endpoints provided. There are four main methods: cancelling a single order, cancelling multiple orders, cancelling all open orders, and cancelling orders from a specific market. To cancel a single order, you need to specify the order ID in the request payload. To cancel multiple orders, you can provide a list of order IDs. To cancel all orders, you can use the 'cancel-all' endpoint. To cancel orders from a market, you need to specify the market and asset IDs. Each of these methods requires a Level 2 (L2) header and returns a response with a list of cancelled orders and a map of orders that could not be cancelled.

Instruction: Explain how negative risk works on Polymarket
Response: On Polymarket, negative risk is a feature that allows increased capital efficiency by relating all markets within events via a convert action. In a negative risk event, a NO share in any market can be converted into 1 YES share in all other markets. This is facilitated by the Gamma API's boolean field on events, negRisk, which indicates whether the event is negative risk. However, there is a known issue with the negative risk architecture, known as 'augmented negative risk', where the outcome universe must be complete before conversions are made, and in some cases, this can be addressed by deploying all named outcomes and an 'other' option or by using a system of augmented negative risk, where named outcomes, unnamed outcomes, and an 'other' are deployed, allowing for trading only on named outcomes and ignoring unnamed outcomes until they are named or resolution occurs.

Instruction: Describe the concept of negative risk on Polymarket
Response: On Polymarket, negative risk is implemented as a feature that enhances capital efficiency by linking all markets within an event through a conversion action. Instruction: Explain how Polymarket handles splitting collateral using Conditional Token Frameworks.
Response: On Polymarket, you can split one unit of USDC into two separate tokens, YES and NO, using the Conditional Token Frameworks. This process involves preparing a condition on the CTF contract and then using the splitPosition() function to split the collateral into the target positions. The amount of collateral to split and the corresponding number of full sets to receive must be specified in the process. If any part of the transaction fails, it will be reverted.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket enables the separation of collateral using Conditional Token Frameworks.
Response: On Polymarket, collateral is split into YES and NO tokens using the Conditional Token Frameworks. This involves setting a condition on the CTF contract and then using the splitPosition() function to separate the collateral. The amount to split and the corresponding number of full sets to receive must be specified. Any failed transaction will be reverted.

Instruction: Explain how token merging works on Polymarket.
Response: On Polymarket, token merging is the process of combining multiple positions to create a single unit of collateral. This operation can occur after a condition has been prepared on the Conditional Token Framework (CTF) contract and involves burning one unit of each position in a full set in exchange for 1 collateral unit. The merging process uses the mergePositions() function on the CTF contract and requires specifying the collateral token, parent collection ID, condition ID, partition, and the amount of full sets to merge.

Instruction: Describe the mechanism of token merging on Polymarket, focusing on the CTF contract and the mergePositions() function.

The mergePositions() function on the CTF contract is used to merge positions, specifying the collateral token, parent collection ID, condition ID, partition, and the amount of full sets to merge.

Instruction: Explain what Polymarket is and how it works, specifically its use as a prediction market.
Response: Polymarket is a global platform that uses prediction markets to allow users to stay informed and profit from their knowledge by betting on the outcome of future events. The platform combines news, polls, and expert opinions to determine real-time probabilities for various events, providing a more accurate and unbiased view of the outcome. Users can buy and sell shares representing event outcomes, creating a market-driven pricing system that allows traders to make informed decisions and potentially profit from their knowledge. Unlike traditional sportsbooks, Polymarket does not have a 'house' to bet against, allowing users to sell their shares before the event outcome is known and making the platform a fair and transparent way to engage in prediction markets.

Instruction: Explain how to fetch markets data with Polymarket in a way that emphasizes the optimal approaches and their use cases.
Response: To fetch markets data with Polymarket, you can use one of three recommended approaches. The first approach, fetching by slug, is ideal for retrieving specific individual markets or events that you already know about. To do this, you can extract the slug identifier from the Polymarket frontend URL and use it to make a request to the Gamma API's events or markets endpoint. The second approach, fetching by tags, is useful for filtering markets by category, sport, or topic. This involves discovering available tags and using them to filter your market requests. Finally, the third approach, fetching all active markets, is the most efficient way to retrieve all available active markets for broader analysis or market discovery. This approach uses the events endpoint and includes pagination to systematically process all available trading opportunities.

Instruction: Explain how clients interact with PolyMarket API in terms of initialization and usage
Response: On Polymarket, clients can interact with the API through reference clients like clob-client (Typescript) and py-clob-client (Python), which facilitate programmatic use of the API. To initialize a client, you must provide the host, key, and chain ID, with options to use Polymarket Proxy associated with an Email/Magic account or a Browser Wallet like Metamask. Polymarket has also implemented utility libraries, such as clob-order-utils, to programmatically sign and generate orders. These tools allow for seamless integration and automation of Polymarket API functionalities.

Instruction: Explain deposits on Polymarket and how to deposit using Coinbase
Response: Polymarket is a platform that allows users to participate in prediction markets. To deposit on Polymarket using Coinbase, users can follow a simple process. Firstly, if you don't already have a Coinbase account, you can create one as described on Coinbase's official website. After creating your account, you can buy and deposit USDC to your Polymarket account via Coinbase. The process of transferring USDC directly from Coinbase to Polymarket is straightforward and doesn't require assistance. However, if you encounter any issues during deposit, it's recommended that you contact Coinbase support for assistance. Instruction: Explain Gamma Structure in Polymarket
Response: In Polymarket, the Gamma Structure is a comprehensive organization model that provides a framework for handling events and markets. At its core, the Gamma Structure is centered around markets, with events and other models serving to further organize and provide additional context. Markets are the fundamental element, with events serving as a collection of markets. The Gamma Structure also considers variants, including Simple Market Polls (SMPs) with a single market and Group Market Polls (GMPs) with multiple markets. Overall, the Gamma Structure is essential for streamlining data and enabling efficient market organization within Polymarket.

Instruction: Describe the Gamma Structure's role in Polymarket's market organization system.
Response: The Gamma Structure in Polymarket serves as a foundational framework for organizing markets and events. At its core, markets are the primary focus, with events and other models providing additional context and organization. This structure also accommodates variations, such as Simple Market Polls (SMPs) and Group Market Polls (GMPs), which consist of a single market or multiple markets, respectively. Overall, the Gamma Structure is crucial for streamlining data and enhancing market organization within Polymarket.

Instruction: Explain how prediction markets are resolved on Polymarket
Response: On Polymarket, prediction markets are resolved by applying pre-defined rules found in the market's order book. When the result becomes clear, a proposer puts up a bond in USDC, risking $750. If the proposal is validated, the proposer receives a reward and holders of winning shares receive $1 per share, while losing shares become worthless. However, if the proposal is unsuccessful or made too early, the proposer loses the bond. Additionally, disputes can be raised within a 2-hour challenge period.

Instruction: Explain the Builder Signing Server in Polymarket and its primary function.
Response: The Builder Signing Server is a self-hosted Express.js application in Polymarket that enables remote signing of builder authentication headers. Its primary function is to keep Builder API credentials secure on your own infrastructure while allowing your application to sign requests, promoting enhanced security with isolated credentials, centralized key management, and reduced exposure.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket handles order manipulation, including orders overview and types of orders.
Response: Polymarket is a decentralized platform that supports various types of orders, including limit orders that can be marketable. To place an order, users must set allowances for the maker asset, and the system monitors orders for validity, tracking balances and allowances in real-time. Orders can be expressed in different signature types, including EOA, POLY_PROXY, and POLY_GNOSIS_SAFE, which are managed through open-source libraries in typescript, python, and golang. Furthermore, Polymarket enforces rails on order placement to prevent intentional abuse, such as blacklisting makers who attempt to manipulate orders.

Instruction: Explain how to check order reward scoring on Polymarket for a single order.
Response: On Polymarket, you can check if an order is reward-scoring using the is_order_scoring endpoint. This endpoint requires a L2 Header and returns a boolean value indicating whether the order scores. You can use the client.is_order_scoring function, passing in an OrderScoringParams object with the desired order ID, to get the scoring status. For example: scoring = client.is_order_scoring(OrderScoringParams(orderId = "0x...")). This will print the scoring status for the specified order.

Instruction: Explain how the Polymarket Bridge API enables seamless deposits between multiple blockchains and Polymarket.
Response: The Polymarket Bridge API allows deposits from various blockchains, such as Ethereum, Solana, and Arbitrum, by automatically bridging and swapping assets to USDC.e on Polygon, which then serves as the native currency for Polymarket trading activities. USDC.e is the bridged version of USDC from Ethereum and is used for placing orders and settling trades. This enables users to trade on Polymarket markets without directly handling multiple blockchain assets.

Instruction: Describe how the Polymarket Bridge API facilitates seamless deposits between multiple blockchains and Polymarket.
Response: The Polymarket Bridge API enables deposits from multiple blockchains, such as Ethereum, Solana, and Arbitrum, by automatically bridging and swapping assets to USDC.e on Polygon, which serves as the native currency for Polymarket trading activities. USDC.e is the bridged version of USDC from Ethereum, used for placing orders and settling trades, allowing users to trade on Polymarket markets without handling multiple blockchain assets directly.

Instruction: Explain Polymarket and its key features.
Response: Polymarket is a platform for creating and trading prediction markets. It allows users to place bets on various events or outcomes, and prices are determined based on the collective wisdom of the market. Users can deposit and withdraw funds using various methods, including crypto transfers, Coinbase, and card payments. Polymarket also offers features such as limit and market orders, rewards for liquidity provision, and a detailed order book. The platform also provides support for users through its API, customer support, and exportable keys for added security.

Instruction: Explain the Polymarket subgraph and its purpose on Polymarket.
Response: Polymarket has created an open-source subgraph that provides aggregate calculations and event indexing for data such as volume, user position, market, and liquidity. This subgraph updates in real-time and can be used to match core data from the primary Polymarket interface, offering a range of positional data and activity history. It can be hosted by anyone, or hosted by 3rd-party provider Goldsky, and is available via GraphQL query interface.

Instruction: Explain how to place a single order on Polymarket's CLOB API, covering the required parameters and possible error messages.
Response: A single order on Polymarket's CLOB API is created and placed using the CLOB Client library. The order is represented as a limit order, but market orders are also supported. To place a market order, the price must be marketable against current resting limit orders, which are executed on input at the best price. Required parameters include the order object, owner API key, order type, and token ID, among others. If an error occurs during order placement, the server-side error message will include a description of the issue, which may include messages like 'order is invalid' or 'could not insert order system error.' Polymarket's CLOB API provides real-time data and supports multiple order types, including Good-Til-Cancelled (GTC) and Fill-Or-Kill (FOK) orders. The API response format includes the success status, error message, order ID, and order hashes, allowing clients to handle orders and errors efficiently.

Instruction: Explain how Polymarket's Resolution Process works with UMA's Optimistic Oracle.
Response: Polymarket leverages UMA's Optimistic Oracle (OO) to resolve arbitrary questions permissionlessly. The resolution process involves several steps, including initialization, proposing a price, disputing the price, and ultimately resolving the question via UMA's Data Verification Mechanism (DVM). When a price is proposed, anyone can dispute it by posting a counter bond, which escalates the dispute to the DVM for a voter-wide vote. The process allows for multiple rounds of resolution, with each round doubling the cost of a potential griefing vector, and also enables market creators to issue clarifications that do not impact the question's intent. Polymarket uses a custom adapter contract called UmaCtfAdapter to interface with the OO, allowing CTF markets to be resolved via the OO.

Instruction: Describe the Polymarket Resolution Process in relation to UMA's Optimistic Oracle.
Response: Polymarket integrates UMA's Optimistic Oracle to resolve arbitrary questions without permission. Polymarket uses the UmaCtfAdapter contract to interface with the Optimistic Oracle, enabling CTF markets to be resolved via the OO.

Instruction: Explain how the Central Limit Order Book (CLOB) works on Polymarket
Response: Polymarket uses a Central Limit Order Book (CLOB) system where traders can place limit orders at specific price points they're willing to buy or sell at. The platform displays probabilities as the midpoint between the best bid and ask prices when the spread is 10 cents or less. This hybrid architecture combines off-chain order matching for speed with on-chain settlement for security, allowing for more efficient price discovery compared to traditional AMM models while maintaining liquidity concentration in active price ranges.

This approach balances speed through off-chain order matching with security through on-chain settlement, resulting in more efficient price discovery and concentrated liquidity in active price ranges.

Instruction: Explain how prices are calculated on Polymarket
Response: On Polymarket, prices equal probabilities and are displayed between $0.00 and $1.00. When a market is created, market makers place limit orders at prices they're willing to pay for YES or NO shares. When opposing offers for YES and NO sum to exactly $1.00, the orders are matched and that dollar is converted into one YES share and one NO share. The displayed market price is typically the midpoint of the bid-ask spread, with the mathematical constraint that YES price + NO price always equals $1.00.

Instruction: Describe the pricing mechanism used by Polymarket
Response: On Polymarket, market prices reflect probabilities and are capped between $0.00 and $1.00. When a market is launched, market makers place buy and sell orders at prices they're willing to accept for YES and NO shares. As opposing offers for YES and NO combine to $1.00, the orders are matched and the dollar is allocated to one YES share and one NO share. The displayed market price is typically the midpoint of the bid-ask spread, with the condition that YES price + NO price equals $1.00.

Instruction: Explain what the bid-ask spread means on Polymarket markets
Response: The bid-ask spread on Polymarket represents the difference between the highest price a buyer is willing to pay (bid) and the lowest price a seller is willing to accept (ask). When the spread is 10 cents or less, Polymarket displays the market probability as the midpoint between these two prices. A tighter spread indicates higher market liquidity and more efficient price discovery, while wider spreads suggest lower liquidity and potentially higher transaction costs for traders.
